      <p>Guatemala is heavily centralized: transportation, communications, business, politics, and the most relevant urban activity takes place in the capital of Guatemala City,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> whose urban area has a population of almost 3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_183-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-183">[183]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The estimated median age in Guatemala is 20 years old, 19.4 for males and 20.7 years for females.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_183-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-183">[183]</a></sup> Guatemala is demographically one of the <a href="/wiki/Youth_in_Guatemala" title="Youth in Guatemala">youngest</a> countries in the Western Hemisphere, comparable to most of central Africa and Iraq. The proportion of the population below the age of 15 in 2010 was 41.5%, 54.1% were aged between 15 and 65 years of age, and 4.4% were aged 65 years or older.<sup id="cite_ref-WPP_2012_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPP_2012-190">[190]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Antigua_guatemala_women_2009.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Antigua_guatemala_women_2009.JPG/220px-Antigua_guatemala_women_2009.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Antigua_guatemala_women_2009.JPG/330px-Antigua_guatemala_women_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Antigua_guatemala_women_2009.JPG/440px-Antigua_guatemala_women_2009.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a>

         </div>Indigenous Guatemalan women in <a href="/wiki/Antigua_Guatemala" title="Antigua Guatemala">Antigua Guatemala</a>.
        </div>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diaspora">Diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>A significant number of Guatemalans live outside of their country. The majority of the Guatemalan <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">diaspora</a> is located in the United States of America, with estimates ranging from 480,665<sup id="cite_ref-US_Census_2000_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_Census_2000-199">[199]</a></sup> to 1,489,426.<sup id="cite_ref-MigrationDC_2006_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MigrationDC_2006-200">[200]</a></sup> The difficulty in getting accurate counts for Guatemalans abroad is because many of them are refugee claimants awaiting determination of their status.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> Emigration to the United States of America has led to the growth of Guatemalan communities in California, Delaware, Florida, Illinois, New York, New Jersey, Texas, Rhode Island and elsewhere since the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> However, as of July 2019, the United States and Guatemala signed a deal to restrict migration and asylum seekers from Guatemala.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Below are estimates of the number of Guatemalans living abroad for certain countries: </p> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable centre"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country</th> 
         <th>2019 </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr bgcolor="ffffff"> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a></td>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Guatemala#Ethnic_groups" title="Demographics of Guatemala">Demographics of Guatemala §&nbsp;Ethnic groups</a>
      </div>

      <p>Guatemala is populated by a variety of ethnic, cultural, racial, and linguistic groups. According to the 2018 Census conducted by the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Statistics_(Guatemala)" title="National Institute of Statistics (Guatemala)">National Institute of Statistics (INE)</a>, 56% of the population is <a href="/wiki/Ladino_people" title="Ladino people">Ladino</a> reflecting mixed indigenous and European heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-205">[205]</a></sup> Indigenous Guatemalans are 43.6% of the national population, which is one of the largest percentages in Latin America, behind only Peru and Bolivia. Most indigenous Guatemalans (41.7% of the national population) are of the <a href="/wiki/Maya_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Maya people">Maya people</a>, namely <a href="/wiki/K%27iche%27_people" class="mw-redirect" title="K'iche' people">K'iche'</a> (11.0% of the total population), <a href="/wiki/Q%27eqchi%27_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Q'eqchi' people">Q'eqchi</a> (8.3%), <a href="/wiki/Kaqchikel_people" title="Kaqchikel people">Kaqchikel</a> (7.8%), <a href="/wiki/Mam_people" title="Mam people">Mam</a> (5.2%), and "other <a href="/wiki/Maya_peoples" title="Maya peoples">Maya</a>" (7.6%). 2% of the national population is indigenous non-Maya. 1.8% of the population is Xinca (mesoamerican), and 0.1% of the population is Garifuna (African/Carib mix).<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-205">[205]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">White</a> Guatemalans of European descent, also called <a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">Criollo</a>, are not differentiated from Ladinos (mixed-race) individuals in the Guatemalan census.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_205-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-205">[205]</a></sup> Most are descendants of German and Spanish settlers, and others derive from Italians, British, French, Swiss, Belgians, Dutch, Russians and Danish. German settlers are credited with bringing the tradition of Christmas trees to Guatemala.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The population includes about 110,000 Salvadorans. The <a href="/wiki/Gar%C3%ADfuna" class="mw-redirect" title="Garífuna">Garífuna</a>, descended primarily from Black Africans who lived and intermarried with indigenous peoples from St. Vincent, live mainly in <a href="/wiki/Livingston_(Guatemala)" class="mw-redirect" title="Livingston (Guatemala)">Livingston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Barrios" title="Puerto Barrios">Puerto Barrios</a>. <a href="/wiki/Afro-Guatemalan" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Guatemalan">Afro-Guatemalans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">mulattos</a> descended primarily from banana plantation workers. There are also <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asians</a>, mostly of <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Chinese</a> descent but also <a href="/wiki/Arab_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab people">Arabs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syrian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian people">Syrian</a> descent. A growing <a href="/wiki/Koreans" title="Koreans">Korean</a> community in Guatemala City and in nearby <a href="/wiki/Mixco" title="Mixco">Mixco</a>, numbers about 50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> </p>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

      </div> 
      <p>Guatemala's sole official language is Spanish, spoken by 93 percent of the population as either the first or second language. </p>
      <p>Twenty-one <a href="/wiki/Mayan_languages" title="Mayan languages">Mayan languages</a> are spoken, especially in rural areas, as well as two non-Mayan <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a> languages: <a href="/wiki/Xinca_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Xinca language">Xinca</a>, which is indigenous to the country, and <a href="/wiki/Garifuna_language" title="Garifuna language">Garifuna</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Arawakan" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawakan">Arawakan</a> language spoken on the Caribbean coast. According to the Language Law of 2003, these languages are recognized as national languages.<sup id="cite_ref-Decreto19-2003_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Decreto19-2003-208">[208]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are also significant numbers of <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a> speakers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_integration_and_bilingual_education">Indigenous integration and bilingual education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Indigenous integration and bilingual education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Throughout the 20th century there have been many developments in the integration of <a href="/wiki/Mayan_languages" title="Mayan languages">Mayan languages</a> into the Guatemalan society and educational system. Originating from political reasons, these processes have aided the revival of some Mayan languages and advanced bilingual education in the country. </p>
      <p>In 1945, in order to overcome "the Indian problem", the Guatemalan government founded The Institute Indigents ta National (NH), the purpose of which was to teach literacy to Mayan children in their mother tongue instead of Spanish, to prepare the ground for later assimilation of the latter. The teaching of literacy in the first language, which received support from the UN, significantly advanced in 1952, when the SIL (Summer Institute of Linguistics), located in Dallas, Texas, partnered with the Guatemalan Ministry of Education; within 2 years, numerous written works in Mayan languages had been printed and published, and vast advancement was done in the translation of the New Testament. Further efforts to integrate the indigenous into the Ladino<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> society were made in the following years, including the invention of a special alphabet to assist Mayan students transition to Spanish, and bilingual education in the Q'eqchi' area. When Spanish became the official language of Guatemala in 1965, the government started several programs, such as the Bilingual <a href="/wiki/Castellanizaci%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Castellanización">Castellanizacion</a> Program and the Radiophonic Schools, to accelerate the move of Mayan students to Spanish. Unintentionally, the efforts to integrate the indigenous using language, especially the new alphabet, gave institutions tools to use Mayan tongues in schools, and while improving Mayan children's learning, they left them unequipped to learn in a solely Spanish environment. So, an additional expansion of bilingual education took place in 1980, when an experimental program in which children were to be instructed in their mother tongue until they are fluent enough in Spanish was created. The program proved successful when the students of the pilot showed higher academic achievements than the ones in the Spanish-only control schools. In 1987, when the pilot was to finish, bilingual education was made official in Guatemala. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Largest cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="navbox"> 
       <tbody>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Guatemala" title="Religion in Guatemala">Religion in Guatemala</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Catedral_Metropolitana,_Guatemala_City.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Catedral_Metropolitana%2C_Guatemala_City.jpg/220px-Catedral_Metropolitana%2C_Guatemala_City.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Catedral_Metropolitana%2C_Guatemala_City.jpg/330px-Catedral_Metropolitana%2C_Guatemala_City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Catedral_Metropolitana%2C_Guatemala_City.jpg/440px-Catedral_Metropolitana%2C_Guatemala_City.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Catedral_Metropolitana,_Guatemala_City.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Guatemala_City" title="Cathedral of Guatemala City">Catedral Metropolitana</a>, Guatemala City.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> continues to remain strong and vital for the life of <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Guatemala" title="Demographics of Guatemala">Guatemalan society</a>, but its composition has changed over generations of social and political unrest. <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>, introduced by the Spanish during the colonial era, remains the largest denomination or church, accounting for 48.4% of the population as of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a>, most of them <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical</a> (most Protestants are called <i>Evangelicos</i> in Latin America) in a wide number of different denominations, made up 33.7% of the population at that time, followed by 1.6% in other religions (such as <a href="/wiki/Jews_in_Guatemala" class="mw-redirect" title="Jews in Guatemala">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Guatemala" title="Islam in Guatemala">Islam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>), and 16.1% claiming no religious affiliation. A more recent 2012 survey reveals Catholics at 47.6%, Protestants at 38.2%, other religions at 2.6%, and the non-religious at 11.6%. </p>
      <p>Since the 1970s, and particularly since the 1990s, Guatemala has experienced the rapid growth of Evangelical Protestantism, whose adherents currently form more than 38% of the population, and still growing, in different denominations. </p>
      <p>Over the past two decades, particularly since the end of the civil war, Guatemala has seen heightened missionary activity. Protestant denominations have grown markedly in recent decades, chiefly <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> varieties; growth is particularly strong among the ethnic Maya population, with the <a href="/wiki/National_Evangelical_Presbyterian_Church_of_Guatemala" title="National Evangelical Presbyterian Church of Guatemala">National Evangelical Presbyterian Church of Guatemala</a> maintaining 11 indigenous-language presbyteries. <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> has grown from 40,000 members in 1984 to 164,000 in 1998, and continues to expand.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The growth of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> in Guatemala has been especially strong, with hundreds of thousands of converts in the last five years,<sup id="cite_ref-EOC3_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EOC3-213">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="Current sources are only orthodox websites (October 2015)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> giving the country the highest proportion of Orthodox adherents in the Western Hemisphere. </p>
      <p>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Maya_religion" title="Maya religion">Maya religion</a> persists through the process of <a href="/wiki/Inculturation" title="Inculturation">inculturation</a>, in which certain practices are incorporated into Catholic ceremonies and worship when they are sympathetic to the meaning of Catholic belief.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> Indigenous religious practices are increasing as a result of the cultural protections established under the peace accords. The government has instituted a policy of providing altars at every Maya ruin to facilitate traditional ceremonies. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:San_andres_xecul_church_2009.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/San_andres_xecul_church_2009.JPG/250px-San_andres_xecul_church_2009.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/San_andres_xecul_church_2009.JPG/375px-San_andres_xecul_church_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/San_andres_xecul_church_2009.JPG/500px-San_andres_xecul_church_2009.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4016" data-file-height="2496"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:San_andres_xecul_church_2009.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A church in <a href="/wiki/San_Andr%C3%A9s_Xecul" title="San Andrés Xecul">San Andrés Xecul</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Between 1990 and 2012, the PROLADES Corporation made a study of public opinion polls in Guatemala.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> Its data reveal a relative decline in Catholicism and significant growth of denominations within Evangelical Protestantism, people adhering to no religion, and minority faiths (including indigenous traditions). In 2018, Catholics and Evangelical Protestants found common cause against abortion, in a rare public demonstration of unity.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> </p>

      <p><i>*Including Judaism, Islam, Mayan religion, etc.</i> <i>**Including other religions and None/NA.</i> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Guatemala" title="Immigration to Guatemala">Immigration to Guatemala</a>
      </div> 
      <p>During the colonial era Guatemala received immigrants (settlers) only from Spain. Subsequently, Guatemala received waves of immigration from Europe in the mid 19th century and early 20th century.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Primarily from Germany, these immigrants installed coffee and cardamom <a href="/wiki/Fincas" class="mw-redirect" title="Fincas">fincas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alta_Verapaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Alta Verapaz">Alta Verapaz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zacapa" title="Zacapa">Zacapa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quetzaltenango" title="Quetzaltenango">Quetzaltenango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baja_Verapaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Baja Verapaz">Baja Verapaz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Izabal_Department" title="Izabal Department">Izabal</a>. To a lesser extent people also arrived from Spain, France, Belgium, England, Italy, Sweden, etc. </p>
      <p>Many European immigrants to Guatemala were politicians, refugees, and entrepreneurs as well as families looking to settle. Up to 1950 Guatemala was the Central American country that received the most immigrants, behind <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, and large numbers of immigrants are still received today.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Since the 1890s there have been small communities of Asians (in particular from <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>, China, Japan, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>) but in recent decades this has been growing. Also, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, the immigrant population is being strengthened by <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> immigration. </p>
      <p>During the second half of the twentieth century, Latin American immigration grew in Guatemala, particularly from other <a href="/wiki/Central_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Central American">Central American</a> countries, Mexico, Cuba, and Argentina, although most of these immigrants stayed only temporarily before going to their final destinations in the United States.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable centre"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country</th> 
         <th>2019 </th>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Guatemala" title="Health in Guatemala">Health in Guatemala</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Guatemala has among the worst health outcomes in Latin America with some of the highest infant mortality rates, and one of the lowest life expectancies at birth in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> With about 16,000 doctors for its 16 million people, Guatemala has about half the doctor-citizen ratio recommended by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> Since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Guatemalan_Civil_War" title="Guatemalan Civil War">Guatemalan Civil War</a> in 1997, the Ministry of Health has extended healthcare access to 54% of the rural population.<sup id="cite_ref-www-wds.worldbank.org_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www-wds.worldbank.org-231">[231]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Healthcare has received different levels of support from different political administrations who disagree on how best to manage distribution of services – via a private or a public entity – and the scale of financing that should be made available.<sup id="cite_ref-www-wds.worldbank.org_231-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www-wds.worldbank.org-231">[231]</a></sup> As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Ministry of Health lacked the financial means to monitor or evaluate its programs.<sup id="cite_ref-www-wds.worldbank.org_231-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www-wds.worldbank.org-231">[231]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Total healthcare spending, both public and private, has remained constant at between 6.4 and 7.3% of the GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-who.int_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-233">[233]</a></sup> Per-capita average annual healthcare spending was only $368 in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-who.int_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-233">[233]</a></sup> Guatemalan patients choose between indigenous treatments or Western medicine when they engage with the health system.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Guatemala" title="Education in Guatemala">Education in Guatemala</a>
      </div> 
      <p>74.5% of the population aged 15 and over is literate, the lowest <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate in Central America. Guatemala has a plan to increase literacy over the next 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government runs a number of public elementary and secondary-level schools, as <a href="/wiki/Youth_in_Guatemala" title="Youth in Guatemala">youth in Guatemala</a> do not fully participate in education. These schools are free, though the cost of uniforms, books, supplies, and transportation makes them less accessible to the poorer segments of society and significant numbers of poor children do not attend school.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> Many middle and upper-class children go to private schools. Guatemala has one public university (USAC or <a href="/wiki/Universidad_de_San_Carlos_de_Guatemala" title="Universidad de San Carlos de Guatemala">Universidad de San Carlos de Guatemala</a>), and fourteen private ones (see <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Guatemala" title="List of universities in Guatemala">List of universities in Guatemala</a>). USAC was the first university in Guatemala and one of the first Universities of America. </p>
      <p>Organizations such as <a href="/wiki/Child_Aid" title="Child Aid">Child Aid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pueblo_a_Pueblo" title="Pueblo a Pueblo">Pueblo a Pueblo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Common_Hope" title="Common Hope">Common Hope</a>, which train teachers in villages throughout the Central Highlands region, are working to improve educational outcomes for children. Lack of training for rural teachers is one of the key contributors to Guatemala's low literacy rates. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Guatemala" title="Culture of Guatemala">Culture of Guatemala</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">

          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vendeuse_de_souvenirs_(Antigua,_Guatemala)_(6941638140).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Vendeuse_de_souvenirs_%28Antigua%2C_Guatemala%29_%286941638140%29.jpg/170px-Vendeuse_de_souvenirs_%28Antigua%2C_Guatemala%29_%286941638140%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Vendeuse_de_souvenirs_%28Antigua%2C_Guatemala%29_%286941638140%29.jpg/255px-Vendeuse_de_souvenirs_%28Antigua%2C_Guatemala%29_%286941638140%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Vendeuse_de_souvenirs_%28Antigua%2C_Guatemala%29_%286941638140%29.jpg/340px-Vendeuse_de_souvenirs_%28Antigua%2C_Guatemala%29_%286941638140%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="801" data-file-height="1068"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vendeuse_de_souvenirs_(Antigua,_Guatemala)_(6941638140).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Guatemalan woman selling souvenirs.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Guatemala City is home to many of the nation's libraries and museums, including the National Archives, the National Library, and the Museum of Archeology and Ethnology, which has an extensive collection of Maya artifacts. It also boasts private museums such as the <a href="/wiki/Ixchel_Museum_of_Indigenous_Textiles_and_Clothing" title="Ixchel Museum of Indigenous Textiles and Clothing">Ixchel Museum of Indigenous Textiles and Clothing</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Museo_Popol_Vuh" title="Museo Popol Vuh">Museo Popol Vuh</a>, which focuses on Maya archaeology. Both these museums are housed on the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Francisco_Marroqu%C3%ADn" title="Universidad Francisco Marroquín">Universidad Francisco Marroquín</a> campus. Most of the 329 municipalities in the country have at least a small museum. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Guatemala has produced many indigenous artists who follow centuries-old Pre-Columbian traditions. Reflecting Guatemala's colonial and post-colonial history, encounters with multiple global art movements also have produced a wealth of artists who have combined the traditional <a href="/wiki/Primitivism" title="Primitivism">primitivist</a> or <a href="/wiki/Na%C3%AFve_art" title="Naïve art">naive aesthetic</a> with European, North American, and other traditions. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Escuela_Nacional_de_Artes_Pl%C3%A1sticas_%22Rafael_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Padilla%22" title="Escuela Nacional de Artes Plásticas &quot;Rafael Rodríguez Padilla&quot;">Escuela Nacional de Artes Plásticas "Rafael Rodríguez Padilla"</a> is Guatemala's leading art school, and several leading indigenous artists, also graduates of that school, have work in the permanent collection of the <a href="/wiki/Museo_Nacional_de_Arte_Moderno_%22Carlos_M%C3%A9rida%22" title="Museo Nacional de Arte Moderno &quot;Carlos Mérida&quot;">Museo Nacional de Arte Moderno</a> in the capital city. Contemporary Guatemalan artists who have gained reputations outside of Guatemala include Dagoberto Vásquez, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Rolando_Ixquiac_Xicara" title="Luis Rolando Ixquiac Xicara">Luis Rolando Ixquiac Xicara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_M%C3%A9rida" title="Carlos Mérida">Carlos Mérida</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/An%C3%ADbal_L%C3%B3pez" title="Aníbal López">Aníbal López</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Goyri" title="Roberto González Goyri">Roberto González Goyri</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elmar_Rojas" title="Elmar Rojas">Elmar René Rojas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Guatemalan_literature" title="Guatemalan literature">Guatemalan literature</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rigoberta_Menchu_2009_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Rigoberta_Menchu_2009_cropped.jpg/170px-Rigoberta_Menchu_2009_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Rigoberta_Menchu_2009_cropped.jpg/255px-Rigoberta_Menchu_2009_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1f/Rigoberta_Menchu_2009_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="304" data-file-height="435"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rigoberta_Menchu_2009_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Author <a href="/wiki/Rigoberta_Mench%C3%BA" title="Rigoberta Menchú">Rigoberta Menchú</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_National_Prize_in_Literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Guatemala National Prize in Literature">Guatemala National Prize in Literature</a> is a one-time-only award that recognizes an individual writer's body of work. It has been given annually since 1988 by the Ministry of Culture and Sports.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Miguel_%C3%81ngel_Asturias" title="Miguel Ángel Asturias">Miguel Ángel Asturias</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> in 1967. Among his famous books is <i><a href="/wiki/El_Se%C3%B1or_Presidente" title="El Señor Presidente">El Señor Presidente</a></i>, a novel based on the government of <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Estrada_Cabrera" title="Manuel Estrada Cabrera">Manuel Estrada Cabrera</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Rigoberta_Mench%C3%BA" title="Rigoberta Menchú">Rigoberta Menchú</a>, winner of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> for fighting oppression of indigenous people in Guatemala, is famous for her books <i>I, Rigoberta Menchú</i><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> and <i>Crossing Borders</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Guatemalan director <a href="/wiki/Jayro_Bustamante" title="Jayro Bustamante">Jayro Bustamante</a> has gained an international audience with his films focused on Guatemalan contemporary society and politics&nbsp;: <i>Ixcanul</i> in 2015, and <i>Temblores</i> and <i>La Llorona</i> (The Weeping Woman) in 2019. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_news">Media and news</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Media and news">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Guatemala" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Guatemala">Media of Guatemala</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Major national newspapers in Guatemala include <i><a href="/wiki/Prensa_Libre_(Guatemala)" title="Prensa Libre (Guatemala)">Prensa Libre</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/El_Peri%C3%B3dico_(Guatemala)" title="El Periódico (Guatemala)">El Periodico</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Siglo_Veintiuno" title="Siglo Veintiuno">Siglo21</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> The <i>Guatemala Times</i> is a digital English news magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> Guatemala also has a few major local channels and radio stations, such as one of Guatemala's major radio stations, <i>Emisoras Unidas</i>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Guatemala" title="Music of Guatemala">Music of Guatemala</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gaby_Moreno_Karlsruhe_Juni_2012_crop_gamma_gauss.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gaby_Moreno_Karlsruhe_Juni_2012_crop_gamma_gauss.jpg/200px-Gaby_Moreno_Karlsruhe_Juni_2012_crop_gamma_gauss.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gaby_Moreno_Karlsruhe_Juni_2012_crop_gamma_gauss.jpg/300px-Gaby_Moreno_Karlsruhe_Juni_2012_crop_gamma_gauss.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/62/Gaby_Moreno_Karlsruhe_Juni_2012_crop_gamma_gauss.jpg 2x" data-file-width="369" data-file-height="354"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gaby_Moreno_Karlsruhe_Juni_2012_crop_gamma_gauss.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Gaby_Moreno" title="Gaby Moreno">Gaby Moreno</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Guatemalan music comprises a number of styles and expressions. Guatemalan social change has been empowered by music such as <a href="/wiki/Nueva_cancion" class="mw-redirect" title="Nueva cancion">nueva cancion</a>, which blends together histories, present-day issues, and the political values and struggles of common people. The <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya</a> had an intense musical practice, as documented by their <a href="/wiki/Iconography" title="Iconography">iconography</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> Guatemala was also one of the first regions in the New World to be introduced to European music, from 1524 on. Many composers from the Renaissance, baroque, classical, romantic, and contemporary music styles have contributed works of all genres. The <a href="/wiki/Marimba" title="Marimba">marimba</a>, which is like a wooden xylophone,<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> is the national instrument and its music is widely found in Guatemala.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> It has developed a large repertoire of very attractive pieces that have been popular for more than a century. </p>
      <p>The <i>Historia General de Guatemala</i> has published a series of CDs compiling the historical music of Guatemala, in which every style is represented, from the Maya, colonial, independent and republican eras to the present. Many contemporary music groups in Guatemala play <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean music">Caribbean music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">salsa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garifuna_music" title="Garifuna music">Garifuna</a>-influenced <a href="/wiki/Punta" title="Punta">punta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_pop" title="Latin pop">Latin pop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Mexico" title="Music of Mexico">Mexican regional</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mariachi" title="Mariachi">mariachi</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Guatemalan_cuisine" title="Guatemalan cuisine">Guatemalan cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:091225_tamales.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/091225_tamales.JPG/220px-091225_tamales.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/091225_tamales.JPG/330px-091225_tamales.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/091225_tamales.JPG/440px-091225_tamales.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:091225_tamales.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Black and red <a href="/wiki/Tamale" title="Tamale">tamales</a> in Guatemala
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Many traditional foods in Guatemalan cuisine are based on Mayan cuisine and prominently feature <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">chilies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_turtle_bean" title="Black turtle bean">black beans</a> as key ingredients. Traditional dishes also include a variety of stews including Kak'ik <i>(Kak-ik)</i>, which is a tomato-based stew with <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(bird)" title="Turkey (bird)">turkey</a>, pepian, and <a href="/wiki/Cocido" title="Cocido">cocido</a>. Guatemala is also known for its <i><a href="/wiki/Mexican_street_food" title="Mexican street food">antojitos</a></i>, which include small <a href="/wiki/Tamale" title="Tamale">tamales</a> called <i>chuchitos</i>, fried <a href="/wiki/Cooking_banana" title="Cooking banana">plantains</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tostada_(tortilla)" title="Tostada (tortilla)">tostadas</a> with <a href="/wiki/Tomato_sauce" title="Tomato sauce">tomato sauce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guacamole" title="Guacamole">guacamole</a> or black beans. Certain foods are also commonly eaten on certain days of the week; for example, a popular custom is to eat <i>paches</i> (a kind of tamale made from potatoes) on Thursday. Certain dishes are also associated with special occasions, such as <a href="/wiki/Fiambre" title="Fiambre">fiambre</a> for <a href="/wiki/All_Saints%27_Day" title="All Saints' Day">All Saints' Day</a> on 1 November, or tamales and <i>ponche</i> (<a href="/wiki/Punch_(drink)" title="Punch (drink)">fruit punch</a>), which are both very common around Christmas. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Mateo_Flores_Guatemala.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Estadio_Mateo_Flores_Guatemala.JPG/220px-Estadio_Mateo_Flores_Guatemala.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Estadio_Mateo_Flores_Guatemala.JPG/330px-Estadio_Mateo_Flores_Guatemala.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Estadio_Mateo_Flores_Guatemala.JPG/440px-Estadio_Mateo_Flores_Guatemala.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Mateo_Flores_Guatemala.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Estadio_Doroteo_Guamuch_Flores" title="Estadio Doroteo Guamuch Flores">Estadio Doroteo Guamuch Flores</a> in <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_City" title="Guatemala City">Guatemala City</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Guatemala" title="Football in Guatemala">Football in Guatemala</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Guatemala and its <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_national_football_team" title="Guatemala national football team">national team</a> has appeared in 18 editions of the <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Championship" title="CONCACAF Championship">CONCACAF Championship</a>, winning it once, in <a href="/wiki/1967_CONCACAF_Championship" title="1967 CONCACAF Championship">1967</a>. However, the team has failed to qualify to a <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> so far. Established in 1919, the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_Federation_of_Guatemala" title="National Football Federation of Guatemala">National Football Federation of Guatemala</a> organizes the country's <a href="/wiki/Liga_Nacional_de_F%C3%BAtbol_de_Guatemala" title="Liga Nacional de Fútbol de Guatemala">national league</a> and its lower-level competitions. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Futsal">Futsal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Futsal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">Futsal</a> is probably the most successful <a href="/wiki/Team_sport" title="Team sport">team sport</a> in Guatemala. Its <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_national_futsal_team" title="Guatemala national futsal team">national team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/2008_CONCACAF_Futsal_Championship" title="2008 CONCACAF Futsal Championship">2008 CONCACAF Futsal Championship</a> as hosts. It was also the runner-up in <a href="/wiki/2012_CONCACAF_Futsal_Championship" title="2012 CONCACAF Futsal Championship">2012</a> as hosts and won the bronze medal in <a href="/wiki/2016_CONCACAF_Futsal_Championship" title="2016 CONCACAF Futsal Championship">2016</a>. </p>
      <p>Guatemala participated for the first time in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Futsal_World_Cup" title="FIFA Futsal World Cup">FIFA Futsal World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/2000_FIFA_Futsal_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="2000 FIFA Futsal World Cup">2000</a>, as hosts, and has played in every competition from <a href="/wiki/2008_FIFA_Futsal_World_Cup" title="2008 FIFA Futsal World Cup">2008</a> onwards. It has never passed the first round. It has also participated in every <a href="/wiki/Grand_Prix_de_Futsal" title="Grand Prix de Futsal">Grand Prix de Futsal</a> since <a href="/wiki/2009_Grand_Prix_de_Futsal" title="2009 Grand Prix de Futsal">2009</a>, reaching the semifinals in <a href="/wiki/2014_Grand_Prix_de_Futsal" title="2014 Grand Prix de Futsal">2014</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympics">Olympics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Olympics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_at_the_Olympics" title="Guatemala at the Olympics">Guatemala at the Olympics</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Guatemalan_Olympic_Committee" title="Guatemalan Olympic Committee">Guatemalan Olympic Committee</a> was founded in 1947 and recognized by the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> that same year. Guatemala participated in the <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_at_the_1952_Summer_Olympics" title="Guatemala at the 1952 Summer Olympics">1952 Summer Olympics</a>, and in every edition since the <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_at_the_1968_Summer_Olympics" title="Guatemala at the 1968 Summer Olympics">1968 Summer Olympics</a>. It has also appeared in a single <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter Olympics">Winter Olympics</a> edition, in <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_at_the_1988_Winter_Olympics" title="Guatemala at the 1988 Winter Olympics">1988</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Erick_Barrondo" title="Erick Barrondo">Erick Barrondo</a> won the only Olympic medal for Guatemala so far, silver in <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_20_kilometres_walk" title="Athletics at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Men's 20 kilometres walk">race walking</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Guatemala at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sports">Other sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guatemala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Other sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Guatemala also keeps <a href="/wiki/National_sports_teams_of_Guatemala" class="mw-redirect" title="National sports teams of Guatemala">national sports teams</a> in several disciplines. </p>
